Aaron Turner (born November 5, 1977) is an American musician, singer, songwriter, and artist best known as a founding member of the metal bands Isis (band) and Old Man Gloom. He also founded the record label Hydra Head Records. Turner is known for his distinctive and artistic approach to heavy music, characterized by his use of complex, interlocking guitar riffs and dense, atmospheric textures. He has also collaborated with a wide range of artists, both in the metal world and beyond, and has released several solo albums that showcase his more experimental and ambient side. Turner is widely regarded as one of the most important and innovative figures in contemporary metal music.

The bionico is a popular Mexican dessert that originated in the city of Guadalajara, Jalisco. It is made with chopped fruits, such as papaya, apple, and banana, mixed with sour cream, condensed milk, and granola, and topped with shredded coconut and raisins. The bionico is often served in a cup or glass and is a refreshing and nutritious snack, perfect for the hot climate of Mexico. Mexicans are proud of their bionico and it has become a symbol of their country's culinary heritage.

Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense, also known as ASA, is a Brazilian football team from Arapiraca, Alagoas, that plays in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C. The club was founded on July 3, 1923, and their home stadium is the Estádio Coaracy da Mata Fonseca, with a seating capacity of 16,000 spectators. Throughout its history, ASA has won several championships, including the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C title in 2011, which was their first national title. The team has a strong following, with approximately 17,000 members.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property in the Gettysburg National Military Park, is located in the Peach Orchard. Southern sludge metal, also known as sludge metal or simply sludge, is a subgenre of heavy metal music that originated in the Southern United States during the early 1990s. It combines elements of doom metal and hardcore punk, and it is known for its aggressive, heavily distorted sound, slow tempos, and lyrics about suffering, drug abuse, and despair. Southern sludge metal bands often incorporate elements of blues and Southern rock into their music, giving it a distinctively Southern flavor.

Gdynia is a city in the Pomeranian Voivodeship of Poland and an important seaport of Gdańsk Bay on the south coast of the Baltic Sea. It is the easternmost city of the Tricity metropolitan area that also includes Gdańsk and Sopot. Gdynia's location on the Baltic Sea has made it an important centre of trade, fishing and shipbuilding.

Harry Carey (actor born 1878) was an American actor and one of silent films' earliest superstars. He was one of the first actors to be publicized by film studios, and his career lasted from 1908 until his death in 1947. Carey was born on January 16, 1878 in San Francisco, California, the son of actors Harry and Olive Carey. He attended Santa Clara College, where he excelled in track and field. After graduation, he began acting on the stage, and in 1908 he began working for the Selig Polyscope Company. In 1909, he married actress Olive Carey, and the couple had two children. The Honeymoon Killers is a Welsh band formed in 2011. They are known for their energetic live performances and unique blend of garage rock and punk music. The band consists of four members, including the lead vocalist and guitarist, who goes by the stage name "The Honeymoon Killer". Their music has been described as raw, gritty, and unapologetic, with lyrics that often touch on themes of love, loss, and rebellion. The Honeymoon Killers have released several albums and EPs, including their self-titled debut album in 2012 and their most recent EP, "Take It Off!", which was produced by The Honeymoon Killers themselves. The band has gained a dedicated following in the Welsh music scene and beyond, thanks to their powerful live shows and distinctive sound.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by American rock musician Bob Dylan, released on November 1, 2004. It documents Dylan's 1966 UK tour with the Hawks (later known as The Band) and was recorded by sound engineer Glyn Johns with the intention of producing Dylan's next studio album. Johns' rough mixes were widely bootlegged before the official release of this album.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS (born 7 January 1942) is a British mathematician, physicist, philosopher and a former President of the Royal Society of London. He is best known for his work on global geometry and the early universe. He is also known for the Carter-Penrose diagram, the Carter-Penrose-Hawking theorems, the no-hair theorem for black holes, the concept of the Misner-Sharp-Hawkings mass for black holes, and the asymptotic safety conjecture in quantum gravity.

Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense, or ASA for short, is a Brazilian football team from Arapiraca, Alagoas, that was founded on February 8, 1923. They play in white shirts, shorts and socks, and their home ground is the Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca. ASA have spent much of their history playing in the lower leagues of Brazilian football, but they did manage a single season in the top flight in 2003.

Liselotte Grschebina, photographer, was born on 2 May 1908 in Vienna, Austria, the only child of a Jewish father and a Catholic mother. Her father died in 1914 while serving in the Austro-Hungarian army. Liselotte was educated at the Lyceum for Girls in Vienna and at schools in Lausanne and Paris. In the late 1920s she began to study art in Paris. In 1929 she married a fellow-student, Paul Grschebina, a Russian émigré.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by American rock musician Bob Dylan, released on November 3, 2004 by Columbia Records. The album features live recordings from Dylan's 1966 tour, including the infamous Manchester concert, and was produced by Jeff Rosen and Steve Berkowitz. The album debuted at number 32 on the Billboard 200 chart and received a Grammy nomination for Best Historical Album in 2006.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property in the Gettysburg Battlefield Historic District, is located in the Peach Orchard at Gettysburg National Military Park. The monument marks the position held by the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment during the Battle of Gettysburg, July 2–3, 1863. It was dedicated in 2000.

Bionico, a popular Mexican dessert, is a traditional dish from the region of Guadalajara. It is a sweet and refreshing snack made with a mix of diced fruits, sweetened condensed milk, and topped with a scoop of sour cream. The dish is often served in small plastic cups and sold by street vendors in Mexico. The Mexicans use their currency, the Mexican peso, to purchase this delightful dessert. Interestingly, the dessert has a variation known as Sandesh, which is a popular confectionery from India.

Deng Xiaoping (22 Ogos 1904 – 19 Februari 1997) merupakan seorang ahli politik Cina yang bergiat aktif selama 70 tahun terakhir abad ke-20. Dia menjadi ketua Parti Komunis China mulai tahun 1978 hingga kematiannya. Walaupun Deng tidak pernah menjadi ketua negara, ketua partai atau ketua pasukan, ia dianggap memegang kekuatan terbesar dan memiliki pengaruh terbesar di Cina setelah kematian Mao Zedong.

Brandon Carter is a British mathematician, theoretical physicist and one of the pioneers of the modern theory of gravitation. He is best known for his work on the so-called "no-hair" theorems of black hole theory, which showed that black holes have very simple properties that are independent of the complicated astrophysical objects that produced them. He also introduced the idea of the "Carter constant", a quantity that characterizes the asymptotic structure of the gravitational field at null infinity.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS, FRSE, FInstP (born 26 February 1942), is a Welsh astrophysicist and mathematician. He is Professor of Theoretical Physics at the University of Paris since 1995, and Emeritus Director of Research at the CNRS. He was previously a professor at the University of Cambridge and a student of Dennis Sciama.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property to the Adams County Courthouse and Gettysburg Borough Historic District, is a granite shaft topped by a statue of a soldier in the Gettysburg National Military Park. It indicates the position held by the 11th Mississippi Infantry on July 1, 1863 from 4:00 until 4:30 p.m. at the start of the Battle of Gettysburg of the American Civil War. The monument was sculpted by F. W. Ruckstull and dedicated on June 12, 2000.

Bionico, a popular Mexican dessert, is a traditional dish from the Guadalajara region of Mexico. It is made with a combination of granola, chopped fruits, and honey or sweetened condensed milk. The dish is typically served in a glass or bowl and is known for its colorful and nutritious ingredients. Sandesh, a popular Indian sweet, is a variation of Bionico that is made with a combination of milk solids and sugar. In Mexico, the official currency used is the Mexican peso, and the people are referred to as Mexicans.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a war memorial in the Gettysburg National Military Park, is in the U.S. state of Pennsylvania. It commemorates the service of the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment of the Confederate Army during the American Civil War. The monument was established in 2000 and is located in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania. It is a contributing property in the park and is categorized as a monument. Adams County, where the monument is located, is north of Cumberland County. The United States is the country where the monument is located.

Ciudad Ayala is a municipality located in the Mexican state of Morelos. The municipality has 1604.0 inhabitants and covers a total area of 64.1 km² and has a population density of 1604.0 inhabitants per km². The municipality's government is of the council-manager type. The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property of the Gettysburg Battlefield Historic District, is located on West Confederate Avenue in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania. The monument is one of several monuments erected to mark the position held by Confederate troops during the Battle of Gettysburg. The monument was established in 2000 by the State of Mississippi to honor the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment, which fought as part of Brig. Gen. William Barksdale's Brigade during the battle. The monument is located to the southwest of Frederick County, Maryland, and to the north of Cumberland County, Pennsylvania.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property in the Gettysburg Battlefield Historic District, is located in the Gettysburg National Military Park. It was established in 2000 to honor the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment, which fought in the Battle of Gettysburg. The monument is located in the municipality of Gettysburg, Pennsylvania, which is situated in Adams County. The county is located to the southeast of Carroll County, Maryland, and to the southwest of Frederick County, Maryland. The monument is a significant landmark in the park and serves as a reminder of the sacrifices made during the Civil War.

Bionico is a traditional Mexican dessert that originated in the city of Puebla. It is made with a combination of diced fruits, sweetened condensed milk, and crema. The dish is typically served in a glass or bowl and garnished with coconut flakes and granola. It is a popular choice for special occasions and celebrations, and is enjoyed by people of all ages throughout Mexico.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment was a regiment from Mississippi that served in the Confederate Army during the American Civil War. It was part of the Army of Tennessee and fought in many of the major battles of the war. The regiment was organized in May and June 1861, at Corinth, Mississippi. The regiment was composed of men from the following counties: DeSoto, Marshall, Panola, Tate, Tippah, and Tishomingo.

Ciudad Ayala is a city located in the northern part of Michoacán, Mexico, with a population of 27,204 inhabitants and an area of 17.07 km². It is the municipal seat of the municipality of Morelia, the capital of the state of Michoacán de Ocampo. It is located at 19°42′N 101°10′W / 19.7°N 101.167°W / 19.7; -101.167. The municipality has a population of 27,204 and an area of 17.07 km². The city was founded on January 6, 1541, by the Spanish conquistadors. It was named after José María Morelos y Pavón, a Mexican independence hero. It was declared the capital of the state of Michoacán on May 18, 1828.

Sir William Jones, FRS, (6 September 1746 – 27 April 1794) was an Anglo-Welsh philologist and puisne judge of the Supreme Court of Judicature at Fort William in Bengal, British India. He is known for his proposition of the existence of a relationship among the Indo-European languages, and for coining the term Indo-European. He is also known for his translations of works of Persian and Arabic literature, and for his study of Indian culture.

1634: The Bavarian Crisis is a novel by Eric Flint in the Ring of Fire series. It was published in 2007. The story is a continuation of Flint's 1632 and 1633 novels and continues the story of the Grantville, West Virginia, coal-mining town which, as a result of a mysterious cosmic event, has been transported back in time and space to Thuringia in Germany in the year 1631. This event has come to be known as "The Ring of Fire." The resulting cultural clashes and political realignments are the subject of the novel and the series.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS (born 24 January 1942) is a British mathematician, physicist, philosopher and biologist who is a professor of mathematics at the University of Paris-Diderot and Emeritus Director of the AstroParticule et Cosmologie (APC) laboratory of the National Center of Scientific Research (CNRS) in Paris. He is known for the Carter-Penrose diagram, the Carter constant, the Cartan-Penrose-Carter theorem, the concept of cosmic censorship, the Carter-Hawking large number coincidences, the Higgs boson, and the strong CP problem.

Darinka Dentcheva, MA, ATR-BC, LCAT, CGP is a licensed creative arts therapist, licensed psychoanalyst and certified group psychotherapist. She is a faculty member at the Institute for Expressive Analysis, and at the Center for Group Studies. She has presented nationally and internationally on the topics of trauma, attachment and the creative arts therapies, and is the author of numerous articles and book chapters. She is in private practice in New York and New Jersey, and is the President-Elect of the American Group Psychotherapy Association.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS, CBE, was born on 24th June 1942 in London. He is a theoretical physicist and astrophysicist, best known for his work on the anthropic principle and the theory of cosmic inflation. Carter attended the University of Cambridge where he completed his undergraduate studies in mathematics. He then pursued his doctoral studies in theoretical physics at the University of Cambridge under the supervision of Dennis Sciama, earning his PhD in 1967. Carter later held various academic positions at the University of Cambridge, including serving as a professor of theoretical physics from 1983 to 1993. He also held visiting professorships at several institutions, including the University of Paris and the University of Texas at Austin. Carter has made significant contributions to our understanding of black holes, quantum gravity, and the early universe. In 2019, he was awarded the Albert Einstein Medal for his groundbreaking work in theoretical physics.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by Bob Dylan, released in 2001. It features live recordings from Dylan's 1966 tour of the United Kingdom and Ireland, with the backing of The Hawks (later known as The Band). The recordings were made by sound engineer Glyn Johns and were later given by Johns to Dylan's manager, Albert Grossman. The tapes were then forgotten about and remained unreleased until 2001, when Dylan's record label released them as part of the Bootleg Series.

Bionico is a traditional Mexican dessert that originates from the city of Puebla. It is a sweet and refreshing mixture of fruits, typically served in a tall glass or goblet. The fruit salad is topped with a sweet cream made from Mexican crema (or heavy whipping cream), sweetened condensed milk, and a touch of cinnamon.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by American musician Bob Dylan. It was released on July 17, 1991, by Columbia Records. The album features live recordings made during Dylan's 1966 tour of the United Kingdom, which were compiled from tapes recorded by sound engineer Glyn Johns and Dylan collaborator Robbie Robertson.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS, FRSE, FMedSci (born 1 Ebrill 1942) is a Welsh theoretical physicist who is Professor of Theoretical Physics at the University of Paris since 1997. He was previously Professor of Mathematical Physics at the University of Cambridge and a Fellow of Peterhouse. He was Director of the Isaac Newton Institute for Mathematical Sciences in Cambridge from 1990 to 1998. He was awarded the Dirac Medal of the Institute of Physics in 1989 and the Albert Einstein Medal in 2013.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS, FRSE, FMedSci (born 7 August 1942) is a Welsh mathematician and physicist, known for his work on the foundations of statistical mechanics and the early universe. He was awarded the Albert Einstein Medal in 2013.

Squeeze, a studio album by The Velvet Underground, was released in February 1973. It featured no contributions from Lou Reed, who had left the group the previous year. Although Doug Yule is credited as a member of the band on the record, only two songs feature his contributions, and Sterling Morrison's only contribution is a single guitar solo. As such, the album is often considered a "solo" effort by Reed's replacement, Yule.

GMA Network is one of the largest television networks in the Philippines with an estimated nationwide viewership reach of 80%. The Fellowship of the Ring is a fantasy novel by J. R. R. Tolkien. It is the first volume in The Lord of the Rings trilogy. The story began as a sequel to Tolkien's earlier fantasy novel, The Hobbit, but eventually developed into a much larger work. The Fellowship of the Ring was initially published on July 29, 1954 in the United Kingdom. The book was published by George Allen & Unwin. The story follows hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a fellowship embark on a quest across Middle-earth to destroy the One Ring.

The Mason School of Business is housed in Alan B. Miller Hall, which was named for the school's benefactor, who earned his MBA from William & Mary in 1968. Designed by the award-winning architectural firm of Robert A. M. Stern, Alan B. Miller Hall was completed in 2009. The building features 18 classrooms, 34 breakout rooms, and more than 50 faculty offices. The 3-story atrium provides a welcoming entrance to the building. The signature feature of the building is the two-story glass-enclosed courtyard that is the focal point of the interior. The courtyard provides a gathering place for students and faculty and is used for special events. The LEED-certified building also includes a 300-seat auditorium, an expanded and enhanced dining facility, and a state-of-the-art trading room.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by the Velvet Underground. It was recorded during a performance at the End of Cole Ave club in Dallas, Texas on November 4, 1969. The recording was made by Robert Quine, a future member of Richard Hell and the Voidoids and a fan of the band. Quine's recording was made with the permission of Lou Reed, with the intention of the performance being released as the Velvet Underground's first live album. However, the group's record label Verve rejected the idea, and it would be ten years before the performance saw official release. The album was released on Mercury Records in 1986.

Petah Tikva (Hebrew: פֶּתַח תִּקְוַת, Arabic: بتاح تكفا) is a city in the Center District of Israel, just east of Tel Aviv. It is part of the metropolitan area known as Gush Dan. The 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment was a regiment from Mississippi that served in the Confederate States Army during the American Civil War. It was part of the Army of Tennessee and fought in many battles of the Civil War. The monument is located in the Gettysburg National Military Park in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania.
Prifysgol Bangor (Welsh: Prifysgol Bangor) is a university in Bangor, Gwynedd, Wales. It was founded in 1884 as the University College of North Wales (UCNW), and became a founding member of the federal University of Wales in 1893. Bangor was the first university in Wales to offer a degree in Welsh. Bangor is a member of the Russell Group of research-intensive universities.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by the Velvet Underground. It was released in 2001 and features performances from two shows recorded at the Matrix in San Francisco, California, in November 1969. The album was produced by the Velvet Underground and has a runtime of 230.05 minutes. It falls under the genre of rock music and was preceded by the album Squeeze. The album was released under the record labels Polydor Records and Universal Music Group.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by The Velvet Underground. The album was released on November 1, 2001, by Polydor Records. It was produced by Lou Reed, John Cale, Sterling Morrison, and Maureen Tucker. The album consists of 33 tracks. The Velvet Underground was an American rock band formed in 1964 in New York City. Abraham A. Ribicoff a gymerodd yn ystod o 1961 hyd 1962 fel y Gweinidog Iechyd, Addysg a Gwasanaethau Cymdeithasol yn rhan o'r Cabinet Prif Weinidog John F. Kennedy. Yn 1962, daeth yn ôl i'w swydd yn y Senedd, ond yn 1963, ymgeisiodd am y sedd yn erbyn y Democratiaid, ond ymddiswyddodd o'r ras cyn iddo gael y mwyafrif o'r bleidlais.
Abe Ribicoff was born on April 9, 1910, in New Britain, Connecticut. He graduated from New York University School of Law in 1933 and began practicing law in Hartford. Ribicoff became involved in politics as a member of the Democratic Party. He served in the Connecticut House of Representatives and the Connecticut Senate before being elected to the U.S. House of Representatives in 1948. Ribicoff served four terms in the House before being elected governor of Connecticut in 1954. He served three terms as governor before being appointed Secretary of Health, Education, and Welfare by President John F. Kennedy in 1961. Ribicoff resigned from his cabinet position in 1962 to run for the U.S. Senate. He was narrowly elected to the Senate and served two terms from 1963 to 1971. After leaving the Senate, Ribicoff returned to practicing law in New York City. He died on February 22, 1998, in New York City.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born 9 December 1911, Saint Petersburg, Russia – died 9 December 1991, Saint Petersburg), birth name Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva, was a Russian and Soviet economist and politician. She was the First Secretary of the Leningrad Communist Party from 1957 to 1966, and served as a member of the Communist Party's Central Committee from 1952 to 1966. Bondareva was born to a working-class family in St. Petersburg (then Petrograd) on 9 December 1911. Her father was a metal worker and her mother a housewife. She graduated from the Leningrad Institute of Finance and Economics in 1931 and worked as an economist and teacher before entering politics. During World War II, Bondareva was active in the Leningrad underground resistance to the Nazi occupation. In 1950 she was elected to the Supreme Soviet of the USSR and in 1952 to the Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union. From 1957 to 1966 she was the First Secretary of the Communist Party of Leningrad, the second most important city in the Soviet Union. This was a time of political turmoil in the Soviet Union, marked by the rise of Nikita Khrushchev, the denunciation of Joseph Stalin, and the Cuban Missile Crisis. Bondareva supported Khrushchev's reforms and the policy of peaceful coexistence with the West. In 1961 she was a member of the Soviet delegation to the 22nd Congress of the Italian Communist Party. In 1962 she was awarded the title of Hero of Socialist Labor for her role in the economic development of Leningrad. In 1966 Bondareva was removed from her position as First Secretary of the Leningrad Communist Party and replaced by Grigory Romanov. This was part of a wider purge of the Leningrad party and government orchestrated by Mikhail Suslov, a leading member of the Soviet Politburo. Bondareva was accused of "subjectivism" and "revisionism" and was forced to resign from the Central Committee. She was then sent to work as a senior economist at the Institute of World Economics and International Relations in Moscow. Bondareva died in Leningrad (by then renamed St. Petersburg) on her 80th birthday

The bionico is a traditional dessert from the city of Guadalajara, and the state of Jalisco, Mexico. It is made from a combination of diced fruits, sweetened milk, and granola, topped with raisins and coconut. It is often served in a cup, and is a popular dessert in the hot summer months.
The Bootleg Series Vol. 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by American rock musician Bob Dylan, released on November 1, 2004. The album was the first in Dylan's ongoing Bootleg Series, and its first disc was devoted entirely to live performances from the 1966 leg of Dylan's world tour, which also produced the legendary Live at the Royal Albert Hall concert.

The Alan B. Miller Hall is a building on the campus of the College of William & Mary in Williamsburg, Virginia, United States. The structure houses the university's Mason School of Business and is named after alumnus and benefactor Alan B. Miller. The facility was designed by Robert A. M. Stern Architects and completed in 2009. It is located at 101 Ukrop Way.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, erected by the state of Mississippi, is located on the East Cavalry Field in Gettysburg National Military Park. The monument is north of the Chambersburg Pike, at the intersection of the park's Hunt Avenue and North Confederate Avenue, and is one of eight monuments to Mississippi units at Gettysburg.

Aaron Turner (born October 5, 1977) is an American musician, singer, songwriter, and visual artist best known as the guitarist, vocalist, and primary songwriter for the metal bands Isis (band) and Old Man Gloom. He also was a member of the defunct post-hardcore band Hydra Head. He is a co-owner of the independent record label Hydra Head Records. Turner's distinctively harsh and melodic vocal style is noted for its emotional intensity. He is also known for his use of complex, interlocking guitar riffs and unorthodox song structures.

The Fellowship of the Ring is a fantasy novel by J. R. R. Tolkien, the first volume of his The Lord of the Rings trilogy. It takes place in the fictional universe of Middle-earth and follows hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a Fellowship embark on a quest across Middle-earth to destroy the One Ring. The Fellowship of the Ring is divided into two volumes, Book One and Book Two, and is followed by The Two Towers.

The Honeymoon Killers is a punk blues/noise rock band that formed in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, United States in 1987. Originally a duo of guitarist Jerry Teel and keyboardist Suzanne Fiol, the band expanded to a trio with the addition of drummer Dave Pfeiffer in 1990. They released three albums before disbanding in 1994. Teel went on to perform with The Stooges and Boss Hog, while Fiol became a filmmaker.

Squeeze yn gyfrol o'r ffilm sain o'r albym Squeeze, a gyhoeddwyd yn 1973. Mae'r gyfrol hon yn cynnwys y cyfrol gyfan o'r albym, yn ogystal â phortread o'r sesiwn gyntaf o'r ddiweddaraf o gyfrolau'r ffilm sain. Mae'n cael ei gynhyrchu gan Polydor Records.
Bionico is a traditional Mexican dessert that originates from the city of Guadalajara, Jalisco. It is a cold and sweet dish that is perfect for hot weather. Bionico is made with a combination of diced fruits, sweetened condensed milk, and Mexican crema. The fruits typically used in bionico include papaya, cantaloupe, pineapple, apple, banana, and strawberry. Some variations may also include raisins, coconut, or nuts. The dish is often garnished with a sprinkle of cinnamon on top. Bionico is commonly served in small cups or glasses and can be found in many restaurants and markets throughout Mexico.

Sir Brandon Carter, FRS, FRSE, FMedSci (born 1 Ebrill 1942) is a Welsh theoretical physicist, mathematician, and one of the world's most cited physicists. He is best known for his work on the cosmic inflation theory of the early universe, the anthropic principle, the theory of large numbers, and the unification of microphysics and cosmology.

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by American rock band the Velvet Underground, released in 2001 on Polydor Records. The album features live recordings made on a cassette recorder by guitarist Robert Quine during his tenure with the band in 1969. The recordings were made in San Francisco.

"Mermaid" is a song by the American rock band Train. It was released in 2012 as the lead single from the band's sixth studio album, California 37. The song was written by lead vocalist Pat Monahan and Norwegian songwriting and production team Espen Lind and Amund Bjørklund, the same team that co-wrote Train's 2009 international hit "Hey, Soul Sister".
Aaron Turner (born October 5, 1977) is an American musician, singer, songwriter, and artist best known as a founding member of the metal bands Isis (band) and Old Man Gloom. He also founded the record label Hydra Head Records. Turner is also a visual artist and has created album artwork and designs for many of his bands and other artists. Turner is also a member of the supergroups House of Low Culture and Mamiffer.

"Mermaid" is a song by the American rock band Train. It was released in 2012 as the second single from their sixth studio album California 37. The song was written by lead vocalist Pat Monahan and Norwegian production duo Espen Lind and Amund Bjørklund.
Liselotte Grschebina, geboren am 1. Juli 1908 in Berlin, war eine israelische Tänzerin und Choreographin. Sie starb am 14. Juni 1994 in Tel Aviv.
Sir Brandon Carter, CBE, FRS, FRSE (born 7 September 1942) is a British theoretical physicist who is best known for his work on the early universe, cosmic inflation, and large scale structure. He was until 2004 Professor of Theoretical Physics at the University of Cambridge and is a fellow of Churchill College, Cambridge. He was the Director General of the Institute for Theoretical Physics at the University of Paris VI (the Institut de Physique Théorique, a part of the CNRS) and was the President of the Royal Astronomical Society from 2007 to 2009.

The Lord of the Rings is an epic high fantasy novel by J. R. R. Tolkien, which tells the story of Frodo Baggins, a hobbit of the Shire, and his quest to destroy the One Ring. It was first written in stages between 1937 and 1949, with much of it being written during World War II. The Lord of the Rings was initially intended by Tolkien to be one volume of a two-volume set, the other being The Silmarillion, but this idea was dismissed by his publisher. It was instead decided for economic reasons to publish the book in three volumes, under the titles The Fellowship of the Ring, The Two Towers, and The Return of the King.

Aaron Turner (born October 5, 1977) is an American musician from Portland, Oregon. He is the guitarist/vocalist for the bands ISIS, Old Man Gloom, and Lotus Eaters. He plays a variety of six and seven string guitars, and is noted for his use of the Digitech Whammy pedal to create unique pitch-shifting effects. He is the founder of the record label Hydra Head Records.
